-Dmockito.inline.enable=true
Το ChatGPT είπε:
You're almost correct, but there's one key clarification:

The line -Dmockito.inline.enable=true is a JVM argument, not a property you put in application.properties. So placing it inside application.properties like that has no effect.

✅ Correct Ways to Use -Dmockito.inline.enable=true
1. In IntelliJ (for running tests):
Go to Run → Edit Configurations → VM options

Add:

-Dmockito.inline.enable=true
2. From terminal with Maven/Gradle:
./mvnw test -Dmockito.inline.enable=true
or

./gradlew test -Dmockito.inline.enable=true
3. In pom.xml or build.gradle (optional long-term config)
You can configure the surefire plugin (for Maven) to always include this:

In pom.xml:

<plugin>
  <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
  <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
  <version>3.1.2</version>
  <configuration>
    <argLine>-Dmockito.inline.enable=true</argLine>
  </configuration>
</plugin>
❌ Wrong way:
# application.properties
-Dmockito.inline.enable=true   <-- ❌ IGNORED by Spring Boot
Summary:
Location	Effect
application.properties	❌ No effect — ignored
IntelliJ VM options	✅ Correct
Maven/Gradle CLI flag	✅ Correct
pom.xml (Surefire argLine)	✅ Correct for automated builds/tests
Let me know if you'd like help modifying your pom.xml or IntelliJ setup.

Yes — adding this to your pom.xml under the <build> section is exactly correct for enabling the Mockito inline mock maker during Maven test execution.

✅ What This Does
<plugin>
  <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
  <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
  <version>3.1.2</version>
  <configuration>
    <argLine>-Dmockito.inline.enable=true</argLine>
  </configuration>
</plugin>
This tells the Surefire plugin, which is used to run your unit tests, to pass the JVM argument -Dmockito.inline.enable=true during test execution.

🧠 Why This Is Needed
Mockito's inline mocking (used to mock final, static, or private methods) requires this flag when used without a mockito-extensions file or when running in environments like JDK 17+.

Without this, Mockito issues a warning:

"Mockito is currently self-attaching to enable the inline-mock-maker..."

And this dynamic behavior will be blocked in future JDK versions.

🔧 Full Example in pom.xml (Minimal)
Make sure it's under <build><plugins>:

<build>
  <plugins>
    <plugin>
      <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
      <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
      <version>3.1.2</version>
      <configuration>
        <argLine>-Dmockito.inline.enable=true</argLine>
      </configuration>
    </plugin>
  </plugins>
</build>
🧪 Result
Now every time you run:

mvn test
Mockito inline mocking will be enabled automatically, no need to pass the flag manually or deal with warnings.

Let me know if you’re using integration tests (e.g., Failsafe plugin) or if you'd like to conditionally enable it for test profiles only.

Είπες:
what does mockito do and why the warning came out
Το ChatGPT είπε:
✅ What Mockito Does
Mockito is a popular Java testing framework used primarily for unit testing. Its main job is to create mock objects—that is, fake versions of real objects (like services, repositories, etc.) that:

Simulate behavior without depending on actual logic or database access.

Verify interactions, e.g., check if a method was called or how many times it was called.

Isolate the code under test, making sure you're only testing one class/method at a time.

🧪 Simple Mockito Use Case
Say you have a service that calls a repository:

public class UserService {
    private final UserRepository repo;

    public UserService(UserRepository repo) {
        this.repo = repo;
    }

    public User getUser(String username) {
        return repo.findByUsername(username);
    }
}
In a test, instead of using a real UserRepository, you'd use a mock:

@Test
void testGetUser() {
    UserRepository mockRepo = Mockito.mock(UserRepository.class);
    UserService service = new UserService(mockRepo);

    Mockito.when(mockRepo.findByUsername("john")).thenReturn(new User("john"));

    User user = service.getUser("john");

    assertEquals("john", user.getUsername());
    Mockito.verify(mockRepo).findByUsername("john");
}
⚠️ Why the Warning Appears
The warning you're seeing:

Mockito is currently self-attaching to enable the inline-mock-maker...
Dynamic loading of agents will be disallowed by default in a future release
is related to Mockito's inline mock maker, which is a special mock engine that allows you to:

Mock final classes and methods

Mock static methods

Mock constructors or private methods (in advanced setups)

To do this, Mockito dynamically attaches a Java Agent at runtime, using ByteBuddy under the hood. This agent modifies bytecode in memory to make mocking work.

🧱 Why It's a Problem
Starting with JDK 17+, dynamic agent attachment is discouraged or restricted for security and performance reasons. So:

Mockito falls back to "self-attaching" the agent, which works but prints a warning.

In future Java versions, this fallback will be completely disabled.

You're being warned to explicitly opt in via the flag:

-Dmockito.inline.enable=true
Or better: configure it permanently (e.g., via pom.xml) for a clean build.

✅ In Summary
Feature	Explanation
Mockito	Java mocking framework for unit testing.
Mocks	Fake versions of dependencies.
Inline Mocking	Lets Mockito mock final, static, private, and constructor methods.
Warning cause	Java agent is auto-attached to allow inline mocking, which will be disallowed in the future.
Fix	Use -Dmockito.inline.enable=true explicitly.
Let me know if you want a clean example of using Mockito in your actual project (e.g. mocking CustomerRepository or BookService).

Here are two clean, safe, and effective JUnit 5 tests for your Spring Boot project. These avoid unique constraint violations and demonstrate meaningful logic:

✅ 1. Test for Customer Creation with Unique Email
@SpringBootTest
@Transactional
class CustomerServiceTests {

    @Autowired
    private CustomerService customerService;

    @Test
    void testCreateCustomerSuccessfully() {
        Customer newCustomer = Customer.builder()
                .username("ronald88")
                .password("testPassword123")
                .name("William")
                .surname("Pugh")
                .address("943 Phillips Row Suite 999\nBarkerbury, IL 25437")
                .phoneNumber("364.208.4476")
                .email("alyssabrown@davis.biz")
                .dateOfBirth(LocalDate.of(1990, 5, 15))
                .isAdmin(false)
                .build();

        customerService.saveCustomer(newCustomer);

        Customer found = customerService.findByUsername("ronald88");
        assertNotNull(found);
        assertEquals("alyssabrown@davis.biz", found.getEmail());
        assertFalse(found.isAdmin());
    }
}
✅ 2. Test authenticateCustomer() Method
@SpringBootTest
@Transactional
class CustomerAuthenticationTests {

    @Autowired
    private CustomerService customerService;

    @Test
    void testAuthenticationSuccess() {
        Customer customer = Customer.builder()
                .username("authuser")
                .password("securePass123")
                .name("Jane")
                .surname("Doe")
                .address("456 Auth Street")
                .phoneNumber("5551234567")
                .email("janedoe@example.com")
                .dateOfBirth(LocalDate.of(1985, 8, 25))
                .isAdmin(false)
                .build();

        customerService.saveCustomer(customer);

        boolean authenticated = customerService.authenticateCustomer("authuser", "securePass123");
        assertTrue(authenticated);
    }
}

Use @Transactional to roll back after test execution.

Assert essential behaviors like saving, finding, and authenticating a Customer.

However, the warning you're seeing still appears because Mockito is dynamically loading the agent at runtime, and the JDK is warning you that this behavior will be restricted in the future.

Είπες:
why we use test? we already were using test without test pom on it
Το ChatGPT είπε:
Great question. You're right to notice that your tests worked even before explicitly adding mockito-inline or other test-specific dependencies like that. Let’s clarify why this happens, and why/when you'd add extra test dependencies like mockito-inline:

✅ Why test-scoped dependencies work "out of the box"
Spring Boot includes a comprehensive test starter:

<dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-test</artifactId>
    <scope>test</scope>
</dependency>
This starter already pulls in common testing tools, including:

JUnit 5

Spring Test

Mockito (core, not inline)

AssertJ

Hamcrest

JSONassert, etc.

That’s why your tests run even if you don’t explicitly declare mockito-core or junit-jupiter—the spring-boot-starter-test handles it.

❓ Then why add mockito-inline?
mockito-inline is an optional add-on to allow mocking of:

final classes

final methods

static methods (via another library)

By default, Mockito does not allow mocking final methods unless you enable inline mocking.

So if you’re doing this:

final class MyService { ... }

MyService mock = Mockito.mock(MyService.class); // ← This fails unless using mockito-inline
Then you need:

<dependency>
    <groupId>org.mockito</groupId>
    <artifactId>mockito-inline</artifactId>
    <version>5.11.0</version>
    <scope>test</scope>
</dependency>
And this in your test JVM config (already added by you):

<argLine>-Dmockito.inline.enable=true</argLine>
🔄 Summary
Feature	Works with spring-boot-starter-test?	Needs mockito-inline?
Basic unit testing (JUnit)	✅	❌
Mocking interfaces	✅	❌
Mocking final classes or methods	❌	✅
Mocking static methods	❌	✅ (with mockito-inline + mockito-inline-extension)
Let me know if you’d like me to check if your current tests require inline mocking.

OpenJDK 64-Bit Server VM warning: Sharing is only supported for boot loader classes because bootstrap classpath has been appended where did i add it? i want to delete this message at all
Το ChatGPT είπε:
You're seeing that warning because Mockito is dynamically enabling the inline mock maker at runtime by loading a Java agent (byte-buddy-agent). This happens implicitly when using recent versions of Mockito without explicitly configuring it. It is not your fault or something you added in code — it's Mockito's internal fallback behavior.

To suppress this warning entirely (and future-proof your build), you have two options:

✅ Option 1: Add mockito-inline as a test dependency (Recommended)
This disables the auto-attach warning because inline mocking will be configured at compile-time rather than at runtime.

Add this in your <dependencies> (if not already added):

<dependency>
    <groupId>org.mockito</groupId>
    <artifactId>mockito-inline</artifactId>
    <version>5.11.0</version> <!-- or latest stable -->
    <scope>test</scope>
</dependency>
Also make sure your maven-surefire-plugin includes this:

<plugin>
    <groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
    <artifactId>maven-surefire-plugin</artifactId>
    <version>3.1.2</version>
    <configuration>
        <argLine>-Dmockito.inline.enable=true</argLine>
    </configuration>
</plugin>
✅ This prevents the dynamic agent attachment, so no more warnings.

🚫 Option 2: Disable Byte Buddy agent logging (Not recommended long term)
If you just want to silence the warnings (without solving the root issue), run tests with this JVM flag:

-Dnet.bytebuddy.agent.silent=true
Or in pom.xml:

<argLine>-Dnet.bytebuddy.agent.silent=true</argLine>
⚠️ This only hides the message — it doesn't solve the issue. Mockito will still dynamically attach, and in future JDK versions this will break.

🔍 Where did the agent come from?
Mockito (or Spring Boot Test) internally triggered this:

You didn't manually add the agent.

It happened because a final class or method was mocked without mockito-inline, so Mockito tried to attach the inline agent dynamically via Byte Buddy.

✅ Summary
Solution	Outcome	Recommended?
Add mockito-inline and enable -Dmockito.inline.enable=true	Removes warning, future-proof	✅ Yes
Just silence with -Dnet.bytebuddy.agent.silent=true	Hides only the warning	⚠️ Not future-proof
Do nothing	Warnings remain, future JDKs will break	❌ No
Let me know if you want me to edit your pom.xml accordingly.

You're still seeing that warning because Mockito was activated automatically, likely due to a transitive dependency (i.e. pulled in indirectly via spring-boot-starter-test).

Here’s a clear step-by-step guide to remove Mockito completely and stop the mockito-inline agent from loading:

✅ 1. Remove mockito-inline if manually added
Check your pom.xml and delete this block if it exists:

<dependency>
    <groupId>org.mockito</groupId>
    <artifactId>mockito-inline</artifactId>
    <scope>test</scope>
</dependency>
Then reload the Maven project.

✅ 2. Prevent spring-boot-starter-test from bringing Mockito
By default, this includes Mockito. You can exclude it:

<dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-test</artifactId>
    <scope>test</scope>
    <exclusions>
        <exclusion>
            <groupId>org.mockito</groupId>
            <artifactId>mockito-core</artifactId>
        </exclusion>
        <exclusion>
            <groupId>org.mockito</groupId>
            <artifactId>mockito-junit-jupiter</artifactId>
        </exclusion>
    </exclusions>
</dependency>
✅ 3. Clean Maven Cache & Rebuild
Run the following to clear any cached mockito jars:

mvn clean
mvn dependency:purge-local-repository
mvn install
In IntelliJ:

Right-click the project → Maven → Reload Project

✅ 4. Check for Dynamic Agent
If Mockito still appears, check for -javaagent or -Dmockito.inline.enable=true in these places:

pom.xml (surefire plugin argLine)

.idea/runConfigurations/...xml

VM options in IntelliJ → Run > Edit Configurations > Test Class

⚠️ Remove any reference to:

-Dmockito.inline.enable=true
-javaagent:path/to/byte-buddy-agent.jar
✅ 5. Double-Check Dependency Tree
Run:

mvn dependency:tree | grep mockito
If anything shows up, it means Mockito is still present via a dependency.

Το ChatGPT είπε:
Your main program (or more precisely, the Spring Boot test context) is closing immediately after your test finishes — this is expected behavior for a JUnit test using @SpringBootTest. Here's a breakdown of what's happening and why:

✅ What’s Actually Running?
You’re running this class:

@SpringBootTest
class CustomerServiceTests {
    @Test
    void someTest() {
        // your test
    }
}
This starts the entire Spring Boot application context, runs the test, and then shuts everything down.

✅ Why the Program Shuts Down
The logs indicate this is a test execution, not your main application (SecurityApiApplication). Spring Boot loads the application context, runs CustomerServiceTests, and when the test method ends, it closes the context:

CustomerServiceTests : Started ...
...
HikariDataSource : HikariPool-1 - Shutdown completed.
This is normal — tests are not long-running apps.

✅ If You Want to Start the Full App Instead
To run your application as a server (not just the test):

Right-click SecurityApiApplication.java in IntelliJ.

Choose Run 'SecurityApiApplication'.

The app will start and stay open as a running web server.

🛠️ In Summary
✅ Your test is working.

✅ The Spring Boot context starts and stops automatically for unit tests.

❌ It is not your main application shutting down — it’s just the test context ending.

Let me know if you want to test full application behavior instead of just unit tests.

You can comment out or delete test classes like this one:

@SpringBootTest

    @Test
    void testCustomerRegistration() {
        // test code
    }
}
Or rename the class to something like CustomerServiceTests_DISABLED to stop IntelliJ’s test runner from recognizing it.

✅ 4. Clean and Rebuild
To be sure everything is reset:

./mvnw clean install
Once you do that, launching your project will only run the main Spring Boot application — and you’ll never see those Mockito or shutdown logs again. Let me know if you want to fully remove the test dependencies from your pom.xml as well.

Είπες:
Something went wrong.

Error 500 - Internal Server Error

Message: An error happened during template parsing (template: "class path resource [templates/index.html]")

Το ChatGPT είπε:
A 500 - Internal Server Error with the message:

"An error happened during template parsing (template: 'class path resource [templates/index.html]')"

…means there’s likely a Thymeleaf syntax error or missing variable/data in your index.html template. Here's how to debug and fix it:

✅ Step-by-step Troubleshooting:
1. Check Full Stack Trace
Open the full error stack trace in the console/logs. It will usually tell you:

The exact line number in index.html

The specific parsing error (e.g. unclosed tag, invalid expression)

2. Common Template Mistakes
Here are typical causes in Thymeleaf:

Issue	Example
Unclosed tag	<div> without closing </div>
Bad ${} expression	th:text="${customer.username}" when customer is not in the model
Mistyped attribute	th:teext instead of th:text
Null values	Accessing fields from a null object
3. Fix Example
Suppose your index.html has:

<p th:text="${customer.username}"></p>
And customer is not passed into the model. Then you get:

Exception evaluating SpringEL expression: "customer.username"

✅ Fix: ensure the controller has:

model.addAttribute("customer", customerObject);
✅ Quick Fix Checklist:
Open index.html and double-check all th: attributes

Comment out suspicious sections and test again

Ensure any variables in ${...} are added to Model in your controller

Want help finding the exact error?
Paste the contents of your index.html, or the full stack trace starting with:

Caused by: org.thymeleaf.exceptions.TemplateInputException: ...
I can pinpoint the bug for you instantly.

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/cart") //Maps all methods starting with /cart
public class CartController {

    private final CartItemService cartItemService;
    private final CustomerService customerService;
    private final BookService bookService;
    private final ChartHistoryService chartHistoryService;

    public CartController(CartItemService cartItemService,
                          CustomerService customerService,
                          BookService bookService,
                          ChartHistoryService chartHistoryService) {
        this.cartItemService = cartItemService;
        this.customerService = customerService;
        this.bookService = bookService;
        this.chartHistoryService = chartHistoryService;
    }

    @GetMapping //@GetMapping becomes /cart
    public String viewCart(Model model, HttpSession session) {
        String username = (String) session.getAttribute("loggedInUser");
        if (username == null) return "redirect:/login";

        Customer customer = customerService.findByUsername(username);
        List<CartItem> cartItems = cartItemService.getCartItems(customer);

        double totalPrice = cartItems.stream()//Creates a stream from the cart items
                                              //Maps each item to a subtotal: price * quantity
                                              //Converts to a double stream and sums them up
                .mapToDouble(item -> item.getBook().getPrice() * item.getQuantity())
                .sum();

        model.addAttribute("cartItems", cartItems);
        model.addAttribute("totalPrice", totalPrice);

        return "cart";
    }

   // @PostMapping("/update")
   @PutMapping("/update-ajax") //updating
   @ResponseBody //Tells Spring not to render a view, but instead return the object (usually a Map or JSON) directly in the HTTP response body. Used for AJAX/REST responses.
   public Map<String, Object> updateCartAjax(@RequestBody Map<String, String> payload, HttpSession session) { //@RequestBody Maps the incoming JSON body of a POST/PUT/DELETE request to a Map<String, String> or custom object. Useful for AJAX (not form posts).
       String username = (String) session.getAttribute("loggedInUser");
       Map<String, Object> response = new HashMap<>();

       if (username == null) {
           response.put("success", false);
           response.put("message", "Not logged in");
           return response;
       }

       try {
           Long cartItemId = Long.parseLong(payload.get("cartItemId"));
           int quantity = Integer.parseInt(payload.get("quantity"));
           cartItemService.updateQuantity(cartItemId, quantity);
           response.put("success", true);
       } catch (Exception e) {
           response.put("success", false);
           response.put("message", e.getMessage());
       }

       return response;
   }

    @PostMapping("/add") //@PostMapping("/add") becomes /cart/add
    public String addToCart(@RequestParam("bookId") Long bookId,
                            @RequestParam(defaultValue = "1") int quantity,
                            HttpSession session,
                            RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) { // Add RedirectAttributes for user feedback
        String username = (String) session.getAttribute("loggedInUser");
        if (username == null) {
            return "redirect:/login";

        }
        try {
            Customer customer = customerService.findByUsername(username);
            cartItemService.addToCart(customer, bookId, quantity);
            redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute("successMessage", "Book added to cart successfully!"); ////This is used to pass flash messages (one-time attributes) during a redirect

        } catch (BookNotFoundException e) {
            redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute("errorMessage", e.getMessage());
            return "redirect:/books"; //The prefix redirect: tells Spring not to render a template called cart.html, but instead send a client-side HTTP redirect to /cart.
            //This avoids double form submissions and follows the POST-Redirect-GET pattern.// Redirect to the main book list page

        } catch (CartItemException e) {
            redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute("errorMessage", e.getMessage());
            return "redirect:/cart"; // Redirect back to the cart
        }
        return "redirect:/cart";
    }

    //@PostMapping("/remove")
@DeleteMapping("/remove-ajax") //@DeleteMapping("/remove-ajax"): This is an endpoint for AJAX-based cart item removal (uses fetch or $.ajax)
@ResponseBody
public Map<String, Object> removeCartAjax(@RequestBody Map<String, String> payload, HttpSession session) { //@RequestBody Map<String, String> payload: Reads JSON payload like {"cartItemId": "123"}
    String username = (String) session.getAttribute("loggedInUser");
    Map<String, Object> response = new HashMap<>(); //Map<String, Object> response = new HashMap<>();: Will hold response data like:{"success": true, "message": "Removed successfully"}

    if (username == null) {
        response.put("success", false); //"Add a key "success" to the map with value true.
        response.put("message", "Not logged in");
        return response;
    }

    try {
        Long cartItemId = Long.parseLong(payload.get("cartItemId"));
        cartItemService.removeCartItemById(cartItemId);
        response.put("success", true);
    } catch (Exception e) {
        response.put("success", false);
        response.put("message", e.getMessage());
    }

    return response;
}
    @PostMapping("/checkout")
    public String checkout(@RequestParam("paymentInfo") String paymentInfo,
                           @RequestParam(value = "checkCardIntegrity", required = false) String checkCardIntegrity,
                           HttpSession session,
                           RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) throws BookNotFoundException {

        String username = (String) session.getAttribute("loggedInUser");
        if (username == null) return "redirect:/login";

        Customer customer = customerService.findByUsername(username);
        List<CartItem> cartItems = cartItemService.getCartItems(customer);

        if (cartItems.isEmpty()) {
            redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute("error", "Your cart is empty!");
            return "redirect:/cart";
        }

        boolean integrityEnabled = (checkCardIntegrity != null);
        //if (integrityEnabled && !isValidCardNumber(paymentInfo)) {
        if (integrityEnabled && !CardValidator.isValidCardNumber(paymentInfo)) {
            redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute("error", "Invalid card number.");
            return "redirect:/cart";
        }

        double totalPaid = 0;
        for (CartItem item : cartItems) {
            cartItemService.updateQuantity(item.getId(), item.getQuantity());

            Book book = item.getBook();
            int remaining = book.getCopies() - item.getQuantity();
            book.setCopies(Math.max(remaining, 0));
            totalPaid += book.getPrice() * item.getQuantity();

            bookService.saveBook(book); // save in both cases
        }

        chartHistoryService.savePurchaseHistory(customer, cartItems, totalPaid);

        cartItemService.clearCart(customer);
        session.setAttribute("checkoutTotal", totalPaid);
        return "redirect:/cart/checkout-popup"; //(URL-based redirection) @GetMapping("/checkout-popup") -> return "checkout" (controller-based rendering)
    }
/*
POST /cart/checkout
→ return "redirect:/cart/checkout-popup"
→ browser navigates to /cart/checkout-popup
→ @GetMapping("/checkout-popup") is invoked
→ return "checkout"
→ renders checkout.html
 */

    @GetMapping("/checkout-popup")
    public String checkoutPopup(HttpSession session, Model model) {
        Double total = (Double) session.getAttribute("checkoutTotal");
        model.addAttribute("totalPaid", total != null ? total : 0);
        return "checkout";  // returns checkout.html from templates/
    }

// History
@Controller
@RequestMapping("/history")
public class ChartHistoryController {

    private final ChartHistoryService chartHistoryService;
    private final CustomerService customerService;

    public ChartHistoryController(ChartHistoryService chartHistoryService, CustomerService customerService) {
        this.chartHistoryService = chartHistoryService;
        this.customerService = customerService;
    }

    @GetMapping
    public String viewPurchaseHistory(Model model, HttpSession session) {
        String username = (String) session.getAttribute("loggedInUser");
        if (username == null) {
            return "redirect:/login";
        }

        Customer customer = customerService.findByUsername(username);
        // Use our new service method to get history for the logged-in user
        List<ChartHistory> userHistory = chartHistoryService.getChartsForCustomer(customer);

        model.addAttribute("historyList", userHistory);
        return "chart_history"; // The name of our new HTML file
    }

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/")
public class CustomerController {

        this.customerService = customerService;
        this.bookService = bookService;
        this.authorService = authorService;
    }
    // Make loggedInUser available to all views
    @ModelAttribute
    public void addLoggedInUserToModel(HttpSession session, Model model) {
        String loggedInUser = (String) session.getAttribute("loggedInUser");
        model.addAttribute("loggedInUser", loggedInUser);
    }

    // Home page

//    @GetMapping
//    public String home() {
//        return "index";
//    }
    @GetMapping("")
    public String viewHomePage(@RequestParam(name = "keyword", required = false) String keyword,
                               Model model, HttpSession session) {
        List<Book> books;
        if (keyword != null && !keyword.isEmpty()) {
            // Fetch books matching title or author containing the keyword
            books = bookService.searchBooks(keyword);  // e.g., uses repository to search in title or author
        } else {
            // No keyword provided, fetch all books
            books = bookService.findAllBooks();
        }
        model.addAttribute("books", books);
        model.addAttribute("keyword", keyword);  // preserve the search term in the view
        return "index";  // Render index.html Thymeleaf template
    }
    // Customer list page
    @GetMapping("/customers")
    public String listCustomers(Model model) {

        return "customers";
        // TODO: Restrict this page to ADMIN only in the future with Spring Security
    }

@PostMapping("/login")
public String loginCustomer(@ModelAttribute("customer") Customer customer,
                            HttpServletRequest request,
                            Model model) {
    String username = customer.getUsername();
    String password = customer.getPassword();
    logger.info("Customer '{}' is attempting to log in", username);
    boolean authenticated = customerService.authenticateCustomer(username, password);
    if (authenticated) {
        request.getSession().invalidate();
        HttpSession session = request.getSession(true);
        session.setAttribute("loggedInUser", username);
        Customer loggedIn = customerService.findByUsername(username);
        session.setAttribute("isAdmin", loggedIn.isAdmin());
        logger.info("Customer '{}' logged in successfully", username);
        if (loggedIn.isAdmin()) {
            return "redirect:/admin/books";
        }
        return "redirect:/";
    } else {
        model.addAttribute("customer", new Customer());
        model.addAttribute("error", "Invalid username or password!");
        return "login";
    }
}
    @GetMapping("/customLogout")
    public String logout(HttpServletRequest request) {
        logger.info("Customer '{}' Logout");
        HttpSession session = request.getSession(false);
        if (session != null) {
            logger.info("Customer '{}' Logout", session.getAttribute("loggedInUser"));
            session.invalidate();
        }
        return "redirect:/login?logout";
    }

    // Admin only

    @GetMapping("/admin/books")
    public String bookList(Model model, HttpSession session) {
        // Admin check
        if (!Boolean.TRUE.equals(session.getAttribute("isAdmin"))) {
            return "redirect:/login";
        }

        // This part for the table remains the same
        model.addAttribute("books", bookService.findAllBooks());
        model.addAttribute("allAuthors", authorService.findAll());

        // --- START: The Fix for Default Values ---

        // 1. Create a new Book instance
        Book newBook = new Book();

        // 2. Set the desired default values on the object
        newBook.setYear(LocalDate.now().getYear()); // Sets the current year (e.g., 2024)
        newBook.setPrice(20.00);                    // Sets the default price to 20.00
        newBook.setCopies(1);                       // Sets the default quantity to 1

        // 3. Add the pre-populated book object to the model
        model.addAttribute("newBook", newBook);

        // --- END: The Fix ---

        return "admin_books";
    }

@PostMapping("/admin/books/add")
public String addBook(@ModelAttribute Book book, Model model) {
    // Check for existing book with same title, authors, and year
    if (bookService.bookExists(book.getTitle(), book.getAuthors(), book.getYear())) {
        model.addAttribute("error", "A book with the same title, authors, and year already exists.");
        model.addAttribute("book", book);
        return "admin_book_form";
    }

    bookService.saveBook(book);
    return "redirect:/admin/books";
}

    @GetMapping("/admin/books/edit/{id}")
    public String showEditBookForm(@PathVariable Long id, Model model, HttpSession session) throws BookNotFoundException {
        if (!Boolean.TRUE.equals(session.getAttribute("isAdmin"))) {
            return "redirect:/login";
        }

        // 1. Get the book to be edited
        Book book = bookService.getBookById(id);

        // --- FINAL DEBUGGING STEP ---
        // Print the ID of the book THE MOMENT it comes back from the service.
        //System.out.println("FETCHED BOOK FOR EDIT PAGE. ID IS: " + book.getId());
        // --- END DEBUGGING STEP ---

        // 2. Get all authors for the dropdown
        List<Author> allAuthors = authorService.findAll();

        // 3. Add the book and authors to the model
        model.addAttribute("book", book);
        model.addAttribute("allAuthors", allAuthors);

        return "admin_edit_book";
    }

    @PutMapping("/admin/books/update")
    public String updateBook(@Valid @ModelAttribute("book") Book book,
                             BindingResult bindingResult,
                             HttpSession session,
                             RedirectAttributes redirectAttributes) throws BookNotFoundException {

        if (!Boolean.TRUE.equals(session.getAttribute("isAdmin"))) {
            return "redirect:/login";
        }

        if (bindingResult.hasErrors()) {
            redirectAttributes.addFlashAttribute("errorMessage", "Copies must be a positive whole number (e.g. 0, 1, 2...).");
            return "redirect:/admin/books/edit/" + book.getId();
        }

        Book existingBook = bookService.getBookById(book.getId());
        if (existingBook == null) {
            return "redirect:/admin/books?error=notfound";
        }

        existingBook.setTitle(book.getTitle());
        existingBook.setPrice(book.getPrice());
        existingBook.setAuthors(book.getAuthors());
        existingBook.setYear(book.getYear());
        existingBook.setCopies(book.getCopies());

        bookService.saveBook(existingBook);
        return "redirect:/admin/books";
    }
    @DeleteMapping("/admin/books/delete/{id}")
    public String deleteBook(@PathVariable Long id, HttpSession session) throws BookNotFoundException {
        if (!Boolean.TRUE.equals(session.getAttribute("isAdmin"))) {
            return "redirect:/login";
        }

        bookService.deleteBook(id);
        return "redirect:/admin/books";
    }
    @GetMapping("/admin/customers")
    public String viewCustomers(Model model, HttpSession session) {
        if (!Boolean.TRUE.equals(session.getAttribute("isAdmin"))) {
            return "redirect:/login";
        }

        List<Customer> customers = customerService.getAllCustomers();
        model.addAttribute("customers", customers);
        return "admin_customers";
    }



}

Το ChatGPT είπε:
The error message confirms a Thymeleaf parsing failure in your index.html, causing a 500 Internal Server Error. The root issue is likely a malformed Thymeleaf expression, unclosed tag, or incorrect syntax.

✅ Steps to Fix the Error
Go to:
src/main/resources/templates/index.html

Check for common Thymeleaf mistakes like:

Missing or broken th:each, th:text, th:if, th:object, etc.

HTML tag mismatches (<div> without </div>)

Use of ${...} outside of valid th:* attributes

Misuse of th:each on a null or non-iterable model attribute (books, etc.)

✅ Example of Common Issue
You might have something like:

<tr th:each="book : ${books}">
    <td th:text="${book.title}"></td>
    ...
</tr>
But if ${books} is not added to the model in the controller or is null, it will crash.

Ensure your controller includes:

model.addAttribute("books", bookService.findAllBooks());
✅ Quick Fix Option
You can disable template cache and enable debug info to get more readable errors during development:

Add this to application.properties:

spring.thymeleaf.cache=false
spring.thymeleaf.mode=HTML

Please paste your index.html content here so I can scan and point out the exact cause.

Το ChatGPT είπε:
Thanks — your index.html looks very clean and structured. The issue is likely caused by this specific line:

<strong>Price:</strong> <span th:text="${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} + ' €'">0.00 €</span>
❌ The Problem
Thymeleaf doesn't support string concatenation using + like JavaScript or Java. This line:

th:text="${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} + ' €'"
...causes a template parsing exception.

✅ The Fix
Update it using Thymeleaf’s string interpolation syntax with pipes (|...|):

<strong>Price:</strong>
<span th:text="|${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} €|">0.00 €</span>
🔁 Final Replacement
Original (buggy):

<strong>Price:</strong> <span th:text="${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} + ' €'">0.00 €</span>
Fixed:

<strong>Price:</strong> <span th:text="|${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} €|">0.00 €</span>
Once you update that line, your index.html should render fine without a 500 error.

Let me know if you want a quick auto-validation for your other templates too.

Το ChatGPT είπε:
Thanks — the error message confirms it: Thymeleaf doesn't allow unescaped literal characters like € inside |...| expressions unless quoted properly.

✅ Correct Way to Show the Euro Symbol in th:text
Use a string concatenation with '€' outside the |...| pipe syntax:

<span th:text="${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} + ' €'">0.00 €</span>
This uses classic Thymeleaf string concatenation (+) — safer and IntelliJ won’t complain.

❌ Don't Do This (causes error):
<span th:text="|${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} €|">0.00 €</span>
Because € inside the pipes without quotes is treated as an invalid character in the Thymeleaf parser.

✅ Final Working Line:
<strong>Price:</strong>
<span th:text="${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} + ' €'">0.00 €</span>
This will render correctly as:

12.99 €
Let me know if you'd prefer HTML entity (&euro;) instead of ' €'.

Το ChatGPT είπε:
You're on the right track. If your index.html didn't change and was working before, yet you're now seeing a Thymeleaf parsing error specifically with index.html, then it's highly likely the error is in the controller logic or the data it passes, not in the template syntax itself.

✅ Here's what to check in your controller and model values:
1. Null or malformed book.authors
If even one book has null authors or a non-list structure, this part will break:

<span th:each="author, iterStat : ${book.authors}">
You should guard the loop by checking for book.authors != null:

<div th:if="${book.authors != null}">
    <span th:each="author, iterStat : ${book.authors}">
        ...
    </span>
</div>
2. Null or invalid book attributes
If book.price, book.title, or book.year is null or in an unexpected format (e.g. non-numeric price), Thymeleaf parsing will fail.

Add safe guards like:

<span th:text="${book.title} ?: 'Unknown Title'">Fallback</span>
✅ Suggested Quick Fix: Add a log in your controller
Add logging to verify what is being sent:

for (Book book : books) {
    System.out.println("Book: " + book.getTitle() + ", Authors: " + book.getAuthors() + ", Price: " + book.getPrice());
}
🔍 Recap Troubleshooting Steps:
Step	What to Check	Fix
1	Any null in book.authors	Add th:if="${book.authors != null}" or guard in the controller
2	Any null or malformed book fields	Add null checks in the controller and/or Thymeleaf
3	bookService.findAllBooks() logic	Ensure it returns non-null and valid book objects
4	Log values from controller	Verify what data is passed to index.html

Το ChatGPT είπε:
Based on your full setup and that all other pages work correctly, the issue is almost certainly due to invalid or malformed data in one or more Book objects, particularly in their authors list or price field.

✅ Immediate Fix – Modify the controller to guard against nulls:
Here’s an updated and safe version of your controller method:

@GetMapping("")
public String viewHomePage(@RequestParam(name = "keyword", required = false) String keyword,
                           Model model, HttpSession session) {
    List<Book> books;

    if (keyword != null && !keyword.isEmpty()) {
        books = bookService.searchBooks(keyword);
    } else {
        books = bookService.findAllBooks();
    }

    // Filter out any book with null title, authors, price or invalid state
    books.removeIf(book ->
        book == null ||
        book.getTitle() == null ||
        book.getAuthors() == null ||
        book.getPrice() == null
    );

    // Optional: log to debug any remaining data
    books.forEach(book -> {
        System.out.println("Book OK: " + book.getTitle() + ", " +
                "Authors: " + book.getAuthors() + ", " +
                "Price: " + book.getPrice());
    });

    model.addAttribute("books", books);
    model.addAttribute("keyword", keyword);
    return "index";
}
✅ Fix the index.html (price formatting):
Replace this buggy line:

<span th:text="${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} + ' €'">0.00 €</span>
With this correct Thymeleaf syntax:

<span th:text="|${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} €|">0.00 €</span>
Or split it for better safety:

<span th:text="${#numbers.formatDecimal(book.price, 1, 2)} + ' €'">0.00 €</span>
⚠️ Make sure book.price is a Double, not null, and not a String.

✅ Summary
Problem	Solution
Null/malformed data	Filter in controller using .removeIf(...)
Invalid authors or price	Check getAuthors() != null && getPrice() != null
Template error on format	Use proper th:text pipe expression
Let me know if you want a sanitizing BookService method to clean your data before rendering.

Είπες:
Operator '==' cannot be applied to 'double', 'null' bad operand types for binary operator '=='
Το ChatGPT είπε:
This error happens because you're using the == operator to compare a double (primitive) with null, which is illegal in Java. double primitives can never be null — only Double (the object wrapper class) can.

✅ Fix the issue properly
If you're using something like:

book.getPrice() == null
That will fail if getPrice() returns a primitive double.

✅ Solution 1: Use the wrapper class Double for price
First, ensure your Book class uses:

private Double price; // not double
This allows null checking safely:

book.getPrice() == null
✅ Solution 2: Safe check using defensive logic
If price is a primitive double, then just skip null check (since it's never null). But if you want to catch zero or negative values (which might be invalid), you can write:

books.removeIf(book ->
    book == null ||
    book.getTitle() == null ||
    book.getAuthors() == null ||
    book.getAuthors().isEmpty()
    // Remove the price null check if it's primitive
);
✅ Summary
If price is...	Use this logic
Double (wrapper)	book.getPrice() == null
double (primitive)	❌ Can't compare with null
✅ Instead: check price <= 0
Let me know if you want to convert your Book.price field to Double safely.

Το ChatGPT είπε:
The ConcurrentModificationException you're facing is caused by modifying a collection (likely books) while you're iterating over it, possibly inside your controller method:

books.removeIf(book -> ... );
This can be unsafe if books is a Hibernate-managed list (e.g., fetched via JPA relations), especially with @OneToMany or @ManyToMany entities being lazily initialized.

✅ Safe Fix: Avoid modifying Hibernate-managed collections directly
Instead of modifying books in-place (like removeIf), create a new filtered list:

List<Book> filteredBooks = books.stream()
    .filter(book ->
        book != null &&
        book.getTitle() != null &&
        book.getAuthors() != null &&
        !book.getAuthors().isEmpty() &&
        book.getPrice() != null
    )
    .toList();

model.addAttribute("books", filteredBooks);
✳️ Contextual Example
Update your controller method like this:

@GetMapping("")
public String viewHomePage(@RequestParam(name = "keyword", required = false) String keyword,
                           Model model, HttpSession session) {
    List<Book> books;
    if (keyword != null && !keyword.isEmpty()) {
        books = bookService.searchBooks(keyword);
    } else {
        books = bookService.findAllBooks();
    }

    // DO NOT modify Hibernate-managed list directly
    List<Book> filteredBooks = books.stream()
        .filter(book ->
            book != null &&
            book.getTitle() != null &&
            book.getAuthors() != null &&
            !book.getAuthors().isEmpty() &&
            book.getPrice() != null
        )
        .toList();

    model.addAttribute("books", filteredBooks);
    model.addAttribute("keyword", keyword);
    return "index";
}
✅ Why this works
Hibernate collections (List<Book> books = bookService.findAllBooks()) might still be lazily fetched or managed internally, and modifying them directly (removeIf) throws ConcurrentModificationException.

Java Stream with filter(...).toList() avoids that by building a new immutable list safely.

Let me know if you'd like me to review your Book, Author, and mapping annotations for lazy/eager loading tuning as well.

Το ChatGPT είπε:
To eliminate the ConcurrentModificationException, you need to update your controller method so it does not directly modify the Hibernate-managed list (books). Instead, filter into a new list.

✅ Step-by-Step Update
🔧 1. Update your CustomerController method — likely in this form:
Find this block (or similar) in CustomerController.java:

@GetMapping("")
public String viewHomePage(@RequestParam(name = "keyword", required = false) String keyword,
                           Model model, HttpSession session) {
    List<Book> books;
    if (keyword != null && !keyword.isEmpty()) {
        books = bookService.searchBooks(keyword);
    } else {

    model.addAttribute("books", books); // ❌ This may trigger ConcurrentModificationException
    model.addAttribute("keyword", keyword);

✅ Replace with this safe version:
@GetMapping("")
public String viewHomePage(@RequestParam(name = "keyword", required = false) String keyword,
                           Model model, HttpSession session) {
    List<Book> books;
    if (keyword != null && !keyword.isEmpty()) {
        books = bookService.searchBooks(keyword);
    } else {
        books = bookService.findAllBooks();
    }

    // ✅ Safely filter books into a new list
    List<Book> filteredBooks = books.stream()
        .filter(book ->
            book != null &&
            book.getTitle() != null &&
            book.getAuthors() != null &&
            !book.getAuthors().isEmpty() &&
            book.getPrice() != null
        )
        .toList();

    model.addAttribute("books", filteredBooks);
    model.addAttribute("keyword", keyword);
    return "index";
}
📌 Why this works
You're avoiding direct removal or filtering from a collection (books) that might be lazily loaded and managed by Hibernate.

.stream().filter(...).toList() creates a new immutable list, avoiding modification of the original.

Let me know if your Book entity contains any cascade logic, or if authors are lazily loaded – I can double-check those annotations if needed.

2025-06-12T22:13:41.255+03:00 ERROR 14728 --- [nio-8080-exec-7] o.a.c.c.C.[.[.[/].[dispatcherServlet]    : Servlet.service() for servlet [dispatcherServlet] in context with path [] threw exception [Request processing failed: java.util.ConcurrentModificationException] with root cause

java.util.ConcurrentModificationException: null
	at java.base/java.util.ArrayList$Itr.checkForComodification(ArrayList.java:1095) ~[na:na]
Το ChatGPT είπε:
Your exception is caused by a ConcurrentModificationException while Hibernate is initializing a PersistentSet, almost certainly related to how you are iterating or modifying an entity's collection (e.g., Set<Author> or Set<CartItem>) during template rendering or controller execution.

✅ Fix in 3 Steps
🔍 Step 1: Identify the Source of the Problem
The key part of the stack trace:

at com.example.securityapi.model.Author.hashCode(Author.java:14)
This means the error stems from your Author class — likely the hashCode() or equals() method — and its use of a Set, like Set<Book> books.

✏️ Step 2: Fix hashCode() and equals() in Author.java
If you override hashCode() or equals() and refer to collections (Set<Book>), it causes infinite recursion or ConcurrentModificationException. Fix it by excluding the collection.

✅ Fix:

@Entity
@Table(name = "authors")
@Getter
@Setter
@NoArgsConstructor
@AllArgsConstructor
@Builder
public class Author {

    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String firstName;
    private String lastName;

    @ManyToMany(mappedBy = "authors")
    @ToString.Exclude
    @EqualsAndHashCode.Exclude
    private Set<Book> books = new HashSet<>();

    // ❗ Do NOT include `books` in hashCode or equals
    @Override
    public boolean equals(Object o) {
        if (this == o) return true;
        if (!(o instanceof Author author)) return false;
        return id != null && id.equals(author.id);
    }

    @Override
    public int hashCode() {
        return getClass().hashCode();
    }
}
✅ Repeat similar for Book.java if Book also has Set<Author>.

🔁 Step 3: (Optional but Safe) Use .stream().toList() defensively in controller
This prevents lazy-loading proxies from being accidentally mutated during iteration.

In your controller:

List<Book> books = keyword != null && !keyword.isEmpty()
        ? bookService.searchBooks(keyword)
        : bookService.findAllBooks();

List<Book> safeBooks = new ArrayList<>(books); // 🛡️ avoid lazy collection issues

model.addAttribute("books", safeBooks);
🧪 Final Check
❌ Don’t use Set fields in hashCode() or equals()

✅ Always create defensive copies if passing Hibernate-managed collections to the view

✅ Restart your app after modifying entity classes to recompile and re-enhance the models

Let me know if you want me to review your full Author and Book classes and patch them safely.

Το ChatGPT είπε:
Thanks for the complete stack trace — the issue is clear.

❌ Root Cause
You're encountering a ConcurrentModificationException during lazy-loading of a Hibernate-managed Set, likely when it's being iterated during rendering or streamed in viewHomePage(). The problem is caused by a bad hashCode() in either Author or Book.

The culprit:

com.example.securityapi.model.Author.hashCode(Author.java:14)
This means your Author class uses Set<Book> inside hashCode() — and Hibernate tries to modify the set during loading, which causes the exception.

✅ Fix It Safely in Two Steps
1. Update Author.java and Book.java
🔐 Avoid using Set<...> in equals() and hashCode(). Only use id.

Author.java:

@Entity
@Table(name = "authors")
@Getter
@Setter
@NoArgsConstructor
@AllArgsConstructor
public class Author {

    @Id
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
    private Long id;

    private String firstName;
    private String lastName;

    @ManyToMany(mappedBy = "authors")
    @ToString.Exclude
    @EqualsAndHashCode.Exclude
    private Set<Book> books = new HashSet<>();

    @Override
    public boolean equals(Object o) {
        if (this == o) return true;
        if (!(o instanceof Author)) return false;
        Author that = (Author) o;
        return id != null && id.equals(that.id);
    }

    @Override
    public int hashCode() {
        return getClass().hashCode(); // consistent and simple
    }
}
Book.java (same principle):

@ManyToMany
@JoinTable(...)
@ToString.Exclude
@EqualsAndHashCode.Exclude
private Set<Author> authors = new HashSet<>();
2. (Optional) Defensively copy list in controller
If you ever do this:

List<Book> books = bookService.findAllBooks();  // returned by Hibernate
books.stream().filter(...).toList();  // ← risk of modifying lazy collections
Then force evaluation safely:

List<Book> books = new ArrayList<>(bookService.findAllBooks());
✅ Restart and Retest
Clean your project

Restart the application

Test the index page

This should remove the ConcurrentModificationException and the 500 error.

Let me know if you want me to review your Book and Author classes directly for a complete fix.

i think i made changes on the models that made it crash
Το ChatGPT είπε:
You're absolutely right — your current model setup is the source of the crash. Specifically:

❌ What's causing the ConcurrentModificationException
You're using Lombok's @Data together with bidirectional @ManyToMany.

@Data includes equals() and hashCode() automatically, which includes Set<Author> and Set<Book>.

When Hibernate lazily loads or proxies those collections, and you access them (e.g., via stream() or logging), it tries to compute hash codes, triggering internal modification and hence the ConcurrentModificationException.

✅ The Simplest Fix (2 small changes only)
To fix it without removing @Data or adding complex code, just exclude the collections from equals() and hashCode().

🔧 Step 1: In Book.java, update like this:
@EqualsAndHashCode(exclude = "authors")
@ToString(exclude = "authors")
@Data
@NoArgsConstructor
@AllArgsConstructor
@Entity
@Table(name = "books")
@Getter
@Setter
public class Book {
    ...
}
🔧 Step 2: In Author.java, update like this:
@EqualsAndHashCode(exclude = "books")
@ToString(exclude = "books")
@Data
@NoArgsConstructor
@AllArgsConstructor
@Entity
@Table(name = "authors", uniqueConstraints = {
        @UniqueConstraint(columnNames = {"first_name", "last_name"})
})
@Getter
@Setter
public class Author {
    ...
}
🔁 Why this works:
These annotations tell Lombok not to include Set<Book> or Set<Author> in the generated equals() and hashCode() methods, which avoids the lazy-loading + hashing trap from Hibernate.

✅ After this:
Clean and rebuild the project.

Restart the application.

Your / (index) and all pages should work without the ConcurrentModificationException.

Είπες:
yes now that i took @data, it worked.explain me what was the issue of the comflict
Το ChatGPT είπε:
Great that it worked! Here's a clear and precise explanation of why @Data caused the crash, especially in your case with the Book and Author entities in a @ManyToMany relationship:

⚠️ Root Cause: @Data generates equals() and hashCode() using all fields
When you annotate a class with Lombok's @Data, it automatically generates:

All getters and setters ✅

toString() ⚠️

equals() and hashCode() ⚠️

🔁 The Problem with @ManyToMany + @Data
In your models:

// Book.java
@ManyToMany
private Set<Author> authors;

// Author.java
@ManyToMany(mappedBy = "authors")
private Set<Book> books;
This creates a circular bidirectional reference:

Book.equals() tries to compare Set<Author>

Each Author.equals() then tries to compare its Set<Book>

Which again compares Book.equals() → 💥 Infinite loop or ConcurrentModificationException

This gets even worse when Hibernate is lazy-loading or initializing collections in parallel, which is what happened in your stack trace.

❌ Why it broke:
@Data made equals() and hashCode() go through entire object graphs, including sets like books and authors.

Hibernate was trying to load these collections while your hashCode was being evaluated (for HashSet, HashMap, etc.).

This led to a ConcurrentModificationException or stack overflow, depending on timing.

✅ Why it works now
By removing @Data, you also removed the problematic auto-generated:

equals() and hashCode() methods

Lombok no longer forces a deep object graph traversal. Hibernate can now safely lazy-load and initialize your collections.

✅ Best Practice for JPA Entities
Always avoid using @Data on JPA entities.

Instead, use only:

@Getter

@Setter
@NoArgsConstructor
@AllArgsConstructor
And if needed:

Write equals() and hashCode() manually using only primitive or ID fields (never collections).

Let me know if you'd like a custom equals/hashCode example that works safely with JPA.
